In this context, it refers to the Typikon itself. So it's fine to say "this Typikon". But the Ukrainian uses "устав" earlier for "general rubric", here it's "цим уставом" meaning "this current Typikon's rules". So "Typikon" is acceptable.

Now the large section "В СЕРЕДУ ВВЕЧЕРІ НА ВЕЧІРНІ З НАПЕРЕДОСВЯЧЕНИМИ" – translation: "ON WEDNESDAY EVENING AT VESPERS WITH PRESANCTIFIED". That's correct. "Вечірня з Напередосвяченими" is "Vespers with Presanctified" (Liturgy of Presanctified Gifts). So "Vespers with Presanctified" is fine.

Check stichera count: "що беруться 28 на 29, бо перша само-гласна повторюється" – translation: "which are taken 28 on 29, for the first Idiomelon is repeated". The Ukrainian "само-гласна" means "Idiomelon" – correct. The term "28 на 29" might be "28 stichera for 29 verses" – translation says "28 on 29", which is literal. Fine.

Refrains: "Приспіви до перших 20 стихир беремо з „Господи, взиваю я”, починаючи від „Впадуть у власні сіті”" – translation: "Refrains to the first 20 stichera we take from 'Lord, I have cried', beginning from 'Fall into their own nets'". The Ukrainian says "починаючи від „Впадуть у власні сіті”" – this is the refrain "They shall fall into their own nets" (Psalm verse). The translation "Fall into their own nets" is missing the full incipit? The Ukrainian has "Впадуть у власні сіті" – the verb "впадуть" means "they shall fall". So "Fall into their own nets" is okay. It's a known refrain taken from Psalm 141:11(?). I'd accept it.

Then: "до стихир 21-ої і 22-ої приспівуємо два звичайних стихи зі стиховні вечірні" – translation: "to the 21st and 22nd stichera we refrain two usual verses from the Aposticha of Vespers". The phrase "приспівуємо два звичайних стихи" might be better as "we add as refrains two usual verses". But "we refrain" as a verb might be acceptable in liturgical translation meaning "we sing as a refrain". However, "приспівуємо" means "we sing as a refrain" or "we add as a refrain". The translation "we refrain" is odd; "we sing as a refrain" would be better. But it's probably intelligible. Not a strict error.

Now, check for missing "Notes" at the end. The Ukrainian ends with "Примітки" (Notes), and the English also ends with "Notes". So that's present.

Now, check for footnote [^549] and [^550] in the source: The given source Ukrainian segment does not have these markers. The translation inserted them. This is likely an error; the translator may have added footnote references that don't exist in the original text at those points. Since we are to check the translation against the given source, those insertions are deviations. So they should be flagged.

Also, the translation includes "[→REF:p121-122]" and similar cross-reference markers. These might be translator's addition for internal linking. However, the source didn't have those. The translator added them. The instructions say "Translate ordinals ... Output only translated text." It doesn't say you can add markup. However, the translator may be using a system where references are marked. I'd consider these added tags as not part of translation if they weren't in the source. But they might be part of the chunk's metadata. I'll note them as additions.

Now, the "ЗАХРИСТІЇ" is "sacristy" – correct. "ТЕТРАПОД" is "tetrapod" – correct (a stand for the cross). "Трапеза" is "altar" – actually "трапеза" in Ukrainian means "holy table" or altar. The source says "з трапези на тетрапод" – from the holy table to the tetrapod. The translation says "from the altar to the tetrapod" – correct.

Now, the veneration at Matins: "одразу по відспіванні тропаря „Спаси, Господи”" – "immediately after the singing of the troparion 'Today is salvation'." This is a clear error. The troparion "Спаси, Господи" is "Save, O Lord". I'll flag it as semantic inaccuracy.

Also check the phrase: "Тропар недільний двічі, Слава: хресту, І нині: богородичний з недільних за голосом хреста." Translation: "Sunday Troparion twice, Glory: to the Cross, Both now: Theotokion from the Sunday ones in the tone of the Cross." "to the Cross" is a bit off. The original says "хресту" meaning (the Troparion) of the Cross (i.e., the Troparion to the Cross). The translation says "Glory: to the Cross", which is a poor translation but understandable. It might be more accurate to say "Glory: of the Cross" as they did for other places. Actually, earlier they translated "Слава: хреста" as "Glory: of the Cross". Here they used "to the Cross". That's inconsistent but not a major error. I'll note it.

Now, check the note: "Службу безполієлейного святого співаємо на повечір’ї." Translation: "The service of a saint without Polyeleos we sing at Compline." Correct.

Now, check the dismissal: "Христос, що воскрес із мертвих, істинний Бог наш" – translation: "Christ our true God, Who rose from the dead". Good, capitalized "Who" for deity. "його" as "His" correctly capitalized. "благий і чоловіколюбець" – "He is good and loves mankind" – correct.

Now, look for any missing sentences: The source says "На вечірні з Напередосвяченими" is translated as "AT VESPERS WITH PRESANCTIFIED". Good. The whole chunk appears to cover all the text.

Potential issues with glossary: "полієлей" is "Polyeleos". The glossary says "Полієлей → Polyeleos". The translation uses "Polyeleos" with capital P? It's used as "without Polyeleos" – that's fine. "Світильний" → "Exaposteilarion". The translation uses "Exaposteilarion" – correct. "Сідальний" → "Sessional Hymn". The translation uses "Sessional Hymn of the Cross" – correct. "Богородичний" → "Theotokion". The translation uses "Theotokion" – correct. "Богородичний з недільних" – translation says "Theotokion from the Sunday ones" – good.

Now, check the line: "Канонів 3 на 14: октоїха недільний з ірмосом на 4, Богородиці на 2 і тріоді на 8." Translation: "Canons 3 [making] 14: Octoechos Sunday with heirmos on 4, Theotokos on 2 and Triodion on 8." The Ukrainian says "Богородиці" (Theotokos, i.e., Canon to the Theotokos), translation uses "Theotokos" – fine. "Катавасія" is "Katavasia" – fine.

Now, the veneration note: "Якщо буде достатня кількість людей, то хор співає стихири поклоніння, доки всі не поклоняться" – translation: "If there be a sufficient number of people, the Choir sings the stichera of veneration until all have venerated". Good.

So the main issues are: 
1. Mistranslation of troparion name "Спаси, Господи" as "Today is salvation".
2. Addition of footnote markers [^549] and [^550] that are not in the source text.
3. Inconsistent translation of "Слава: хресту" as "Glory: to the Cross" instead of "of the Cross".
4. Addition of cross-reference tags like "[→REF:p121-122]" not present in source.

But note that the cross-reference tags might be acceptable if they are a translation system feature, but per the strict "output only translated text" rule, they should not be added. I'll flag them.

Now output findings as concise markdown list.

### Audit Findings
**Audit Findings**

- **Semantic Inaccuracy (Mistranslation):** At Matins for the Veneration of the Cross, the troparion incipit `„Спаси, Господи”` is rendered as “Today is salvation.” This is incorrect; it should be “Save, O Lord” (or the full “Save, O Lord, Thy people”). The Ukrainian refers to the troparion of the Cross, not to a different hymn.

- **Added Footnote Markers not in Original:** The translation inserts inline footnote numbers `[^549]` and `[^550]` that are absent from the provided Ukrainian source at those points (the note on p. 127 and “fifth Sunday of Lent”). Unless the source contains superscript footnote markers not shown in the segment, these are unwarranted additions that violate the strict 1:1 content rule.

- **Added Cross‑Reference Tags:** The translation includes bracketed directive tags like `[→REF:p121‑122]`, `[→REF:p122‑123]`, `[→REF:p124‑127]`. These are not present in the Ukrainian text and constitute added markup, contrary to the instruction to “output only translated text.”

- **Inconsistent Rendering of `Слава: хресту`:** In the section *AT Great Matins*, “Glory: to the Cross” is used, whereas elsewhere the same construction is correctly translated as “Glory: of the Cross” (e.g., “Слава: хреста” → “Glory: of the Cross”). Liturgical English normally uses “Glory … of the Cross”; the inconsistent “to the Cross” is a minor stylistic deviation.

- **Minor Terminology:** No glossary term violations were found. “Prokimenon,” “Theotokion,” “Sessional Hymn,” “Exaposteilarion,” “Idiomelon,” “Aposticha,” “Polyeleos,” “Katavasia,” and “Heirmos” are used correctly. Divine pronouns and capitalization (e.g., “Who rose from the dead,” “His most pure Mother”) are proper.

Now Квітна Неділя (Flowery Sunday, i.e., Palm Sunday). Source: "КВІТНА НЕДІЛЯ" -> "FLOWER SUNDAY". The translation also adds footnote [^562] before "Everything". That's fine.

"Все – за загальним уставом господнього свята зі все-нічним без посвяття. Має все своє окреме, а на Літургії – антифони і вхідне. Одначе, перед тропарем Квітної співаємо вчорашній тропар Лазаря; тільки по великому славослов’ї співаємо тропар Лазаря один." Translation: "Everything - according to the general rubric of a feast of the Lord with All-Night Vigil without Litiya. It has everything proper to itself, and at the Liturgy - Antiphons and Entrance Hymn. However, before the Troparion of Flowery [Sunday] we sing yesterday's Troparion of Lazarus; only after the Great Doxology we sing the Troparion of Lazarus alone."

Note: "без посвяття" means "without Afterfeast" (посвяття = Afterfeast). But translation says "without Litiya"? That's wrong. посвяття is Afterfeast, not Litiya. Litiya is Літія. So this is a mistranslation. The phrase "зі все-нічним без посвяття" means "with All-Night Vigil without Afterfeast". Because Palm Sunday, a feast of the Lord, does not have an Afterfeast period. So translation says "without Litiya" which is incorrect. The source says "без посвяття". So error: mistranslation of посвяття as Litiya.

Next, "a на Літургії – антифони і вхідне" -> "and at the Liturgy - Antiphons and Entrance Hymn". "Entry verse"? Actually "вхідне" could be the Entrance Hymn (the troparion at the entrance). That's fine.

Then the note about singing Troparion of Lazarus: translation "only after the Great Doxology we sing the Troparion of Lazarus alone." That's fine.

Then the Vespers: "НА ВЕЛИКІЙ ВЕЧІРНІ: На „Господи, взиваю я” – стихири на 10; і на благословенні хлібів – тропар Лазаря двічі і Квітної – раз." -> "AT Great Vespers: On "Lord, I have cried" - stichera on 10; and at the blessing of loaves - Troparion of Lazarus twice and of Flowery [Sunday] - once." 2. The blessing and distribution of branches paragraph. We need to check for accuracy. Source: "Благословення і роздавання галузок відбувається, за уставом, одразу по 50-му псалмі, під час цілування Євангелії. За нашим звичаєм, благословення відбувається по 50-му псалмі, а роздавання – під час помазання єлеєм (мирування), тобто під час канону. А відбувається так: Коли ієрей відспіває Євангелію, кладе її на аналогій поблизу тетраподу, між двома запаленими на свічниках свічами. На тетраподі покладені галузки і підготовані кадильниці і кропильниці. Ієрей підходить до тетраподу і в час, коли хор читає 50-й псалом, насипав і поблагословив кадило, кадить галузки від чотирьох боків тетраподу і, по закінченні 50-го псалма, коли диякон виголосить (якщо його не буде, то сам ієрей) „Господеві помолімся”, читає голосно (зі служебника або з тріоді ) першу молитву „Господи, Боже наш”, а хор відповідає: „Амінь”. Ієрей: „Мир всім”; диякон: „Голови ваші перед Господом схиліть”; і, по „Тобі, Господи”, ієрей читає другу молитву „Господи Боже Вседержителю ... і на віки вічні” ; хор: „Амінь”; ієрей кропить свяченою водою галузки, промовляючи: „Благословляються і освячуються” та ін; і, після відспівання єктенії „Спаси, Боже”, правицею помазує людей, а лівою рукою роздає всім галузки, які поважно подає йому диякон, а якщо диякона не буде, то один з церковних служителів ."

Translation: "The blessing and distribution of branches takes place, according to the rubric, immediately after the 50th Psalm, during the kissing of the Gospel. According to our custom, the blessing takes place after the 50th Psalm, and the distribution - during the anointing with oil (myrovanie), that is during the canon. And it takes place thus: When the Priest has sung the Gospel, he places it on the analogion near the tetrapod, between two candles lit on candlesticks. On the tetrapod are placed branches and prepared censers and sprinklers. The Priest approaches the tetrapod and at the time when the Choir reads the 50th Psalm, having put incense in and blessed the censer, censes the branches from the four sides of the tetrapod and, after the conclusion of the 50th Psalm, when the Deacon exclaims (if there be none, then the Priest himself) "Let us pray to the Lord", reads aloud (from the Sluzhebnik (lit. "Service Book") or from the Triodion[^563] ) the first prayer "O Lord our God", and the Choir responds: "Amen". Priest: "Peace be to all"; deacon: "Bow your heads unto the Lord"; and, after "To Thee, O Lord", the Priest reads the second prayer "O Lord God Almighty... unto ages of ages"[^564]; choir: "Amen"; the Priest sprinkles the branches with holy water, saying: "These branches are blessed and sanctified" and the rest; and, after singing the litany "Save, O God", with His right hand anoints the people, and with His left hand distributes to all the branches, which the Deacon solemnly hands to him, and if there be no deacon, then one of the church servers[^565]."

Check for liturgical terms: "єлей" -> oil, correctly. The translation adds footnote markers. There's a potential pronoun issue: "with His right hand anoints the people" – "His" capitalized referring to the priest? In liturgical texts, sometimes the priest's actions are not capitalized. But the rule is: Deity capitalization: strictly capitalize all pronouns referring to Deity. But here "His right hand" refers to the priest, not God. So it should not be capitalized. In the original, it's "правицею помазує людей" — the priest anoints, no need to capitalize "His". The translation writes "with His right hand anoints", which incorrectly capitalizes the pronoun referring to the priest. This violates deity capitalization rule. Also later "the Deacon solemnly hands to him" – that's fine. So there's an error: capitalization of "His" when not referring to God. Possibly the translator thought it referred to Christ? But here the priest anoints people with his right hand. So should be "with his right hand". That's a violation.

Also the text of the prayer "These branches are blessed and sanctified" might be the actual prayer. That's fine.

### Audit Findings
### Audit Findings

- **Mistranslation of liturgical term:** "without Litiya" → should be "without Afterfeast". The term *посвяття* (Afterfeast) was incorrectly translated as "Litiya" (Літія), which is a different service.  *(Glossary: Посвяття = Afterfeast)*.

- **Deity capitalization violation:** "with His right hand anoints" uses a capitalized pronoun referring to the priest, not the Deity. Should be lowercase: "with his right hand anoints".

**No other missing sentences or semantic inaccuracies identified.**

"Now lettest Thou Thy servant depart" is the Song of Simeon, correct. "Virgin Theotokos" is a troparion, fine.

Now, "НА ПОВЕЧІР’Ї: В неділю ввечері співаємо мале повечір’я, за уставом інших неділь Великого посту, і на ньому – трипіснець тріоді, а по трисвятому – кондак тріоді один." Translation: "On Sunday evening we sing Small Compline, according to the rubric of other Sundays of Great Lent, and at it - the triodion of the Triodion, and after the Trisagion - Kontakion of the Triodion only." Again "triodion" for "трипіснець". So error.

Similarly, "В понеділок і вівторок увечері – велике повечір’я з поклонами за пісним уставом, а на ньому також – трипіснець тріоді і по трисвятому – кондак тріоді, відтак „Господи сил, будь з нами” ." Translation: "On Monday and Tuesday evening - Great Compline with prostrations according to the Lenten rubric, and at it also - the triodion of the Triodion and after the Trisagion - Kontakion of the Triodion, then "O Lord of Hosts, be with us"[^568]." Again error.

Then "В середу ввечері співаємо мале повечір’я , також і на ньому – трипіснець тріоді і, по трисвятому, – кондак тріоді один." Translation: "On Wednesday evening we sing Small Compline[^569], also at it - the triodion of the Triodion and, after the Trisagion, - Kontakion of the Triodion only." Again error.

So the main terminology error is translating трипіснець as triodion instead of triode (or three-ode canon). Also the phrase "the triodion of the Triodion" is awkward and wrong. We need to flag.

Now, check Matins: "Канон тільки один: трипіснець в понеділок і середу, або двопіснець у вівторок." Translation: "Canon only one: triodion on Monday and Wednesday, or diodion [two-ode canon] on Tuesday." Again "triodion" for "трипіснець". That should be "triode" or "three-ode canon". They used "diodion" with gloss, but not "triodion". That's inconsistent and wrong. So we flag.

Now, "тропарі – на 12, ірмоси – по двічі." - correct.

Now, "Пісень не відмовляємо" – they translated as "We do not recite the [Biblical] Odes". Good.

Now, "Ірмос канону раз обидва хори разом." – "heirmos of the canon once both choirs together." Good.

Now, "Світильний „Світлицю твою”" – Exaposteilarion "Thy bridal chamber". Good.

Now, "Хвалитних стихир – 4: тріоді, Слава, і нині: тріоді, мале славослов’я і, по „Сповнім”, – стиховня тріоді та все інше з поклонами, як в пісні дні Великого посту." Translation: "Stichera of the Praises - 4: of the Triodion, Glory, Both now: Triodion, Small Doxology and, after "Let us complete", - Aposticha of the Triodion and everything else with prostrations, as on the Lenten days of Great Lent." Correct. "Let us complete" is a part of the litany "Let us complete our evening prayer". The phrase "Сповнім" is the beginning of the litany: "Сповнім вечірню молитву нашу Господеві." Yes.

Now, "НА ЧАСАХ": "Все – за загальним пісним уставом Великого посту, тільки:" Translation: "Everything - according to the general Lenten rubric of Great Lent, only:" Good.

Now, "На 1-му і 9-му часах катизми не буде, а буде лише на 3-му і 6-му." Translation: "At the 1st and 9th Hours there will be no Kathisma, but it will be only at the 3rd and 6th." Good.

Now, "Безпосередньо після богородичного „Богородице, ти лоза” на 3-му часі і, після відповідних богородичних, на інших двох часах, устави приписують читання Тетроєвангелії, яка сьогодні у нас читається тільки по катедральних, або соборних, церквах ." Translation: "Immediately after the Theotokion "O Theotokos, Thou Art the vine" at the 3rd Hour and, after the corresponding Theotokia, at the other two Hours, the rubrics prescribe the reading of the Four Gospels, which today among us is read only in cathedral, or conciliar, churches[^573]." Good. They capitalized "Thou Art the vine" properly. "Тетроєвангелії" – Four Gospels, yes. "катедральних, або соборних, церквах" – "cathedral, or conciliar, churches" – fine.

Now, "На 6-му часі Євангелію читаємо не відразу після богородичного, а по закінченні тропаря пророцтва і паремії з її прокіменами." Translation: "At the 6th Hour we read the Gospel not immediately after the Theotokion, but after the conclusion of the Troparion of the Prophecy and the Paremia with its Prokimena." Good. "Paremia" from паремія, that's standard.

Now, "Читання Четверо-євангелії охоплює всіх євангелистів, тобто Матея, Марка і Луку цілих, а Івана – тільки до „Страстей Христових”, тобто до „Нині прославився”, зас. 46, пісня 13.32." Translation: "The reading of the Four Gospels covers all the Evangelists, that is Matthew, Mark and Luke in full, and John - only up to the "Passion of Christ", that is up to "Now is the Son of man glorified", Section 46, verse 13.32." Good. They added "the Son of man" as previously discussed, acceptable.

Now, "Всі євангелисти, разом взяті, поділені на 9 читань, за числом трьох часів (3, 6, 9) і трьох днів (понеділок, вівторок, середа)." Translation: "All the Evangelists, taken together, are divided into 9 readings, according to the number of the three Hours (3, 6, 9) and three days (Monday, Tuesday, Wednesday)." Good.

Now, "Матея поділено на 2 читання, Марка – на 2, Івана – на 2, а Луку – на 3." Trans: "Matthew is divided into 2 readings, Mark - into 2, John - into 2, and Luke - into 3." Good.

Now, descriptions of first half etc. are accurate.

Now, "Устав не зазначає, де закінчується перша половина трьох євангелистів і перша та друга частини Луки." Trans: "The rubric does not indicate where the first half of the three Evangelists and the first and second parts of Luke end." Good.

Now, "Але оскільки Матея має 28 пісень, то половина її закінчується 14-ою піснею, Марка – 16 пісень, то половина її закінчується 8-ою піснею, Луки – 24 пісні, то перша її частина закінчується 8-ою піснею, а друга – 16-ою. Івана, до „Нині прославився”, має 12 пісень і частину 13-ої пісні, тому її половина закінчується 6-ою піснею і частиною 7-ої." Translation: "But since Matthew has 28 chapters, its half ends with the 14th chapter, Mark - 16 chapters, so its half ends with the 8th chapter, Luke - 24 chapters, so its first part ends with the 8th chapter, and the second - with the 16th. John, up to "Now is [the Son of man] glorified", has 12 chapters and part of the 13th chapter, therefore its half ends with the 6th chapter and part of the 7th." Good. The translation adds "[the Son of man]" in brackets, which is fine.

Now, "Ієрей, на початку кожного читання, убраний у фелон пісної барви, відчиняє святі двері і кадить все за звичаєм, відтак, вийшовши святими дверми до аналоя, поставленого перед святими дверми напроти людей, на якому стоять два свічники з запаленими свічками, читає звідти Євангелію, починаючи від „І щоб удостоїтися нам”. По закінченні кожного читання, поцілувавши початок читання і залишивши Євангелію на аналої до закінчення 3-го читання, повертається до святилища і, зачинивши святі двері, скидає фелон ." Translation: "The Priest, at the beginning of each reading, dressed in a phelonion of Lenten color, opens the holy doors and censes everything as usual, then, having come out through the holy doors to the analogion placed before the holy doors facing the people, on which stand two candlesticks with lit candles, reads from there the Gospel, beginning from "And that we may be accounted worthy". After the conclusion of each reading, having kissed the beginning of the reading and leaving the Gospel on the analogion until the end of the 3rd reading, he returns to the sanctuary and, having closed the holy doors, takes off the phelonion[^574]." Very accurate. "санктуарій" – "sanctuary", correct.

Now, "По трисвятому – кондак тріоді." Trans: "After the Trisagion - Kontakion of the Triodion." Good.

Now, "НА ОБІДНИЦІ: Тільки один кондак тріоді." Trans: "AT THE TYPIKA: Only one Kontakion of the Triodion." Good.

So the only substantial error is the mis-translation of "трипіснець" as "triodion". Also the footnote gap.

### Audit Findings
**Audit Findings**

- **Terminology Error (Mis-translation of *трипіснець*)**  
  The Ukrainian term *трипіснець* (three‑ode canon) is consistently rendered as *triodion*, which refers to the liturgical book, not the canon type. This creates misleading phrases like “the triodion of the Triodion” (at Compline and Matins).  
  ➤ **Required**: Use **triode** (or **three‑ode canon**) for *трипіснець*.  
  *Examples*: “the triode of the Triodion”, “Canon only one: triode on Monday and Wednesday”.

- **Missing Footnote Marker**  
  The translation jumps from `[^571]` to `[^573]`, skipping `[^572]`. The source text likely contains a footnote at that point; the omission may leave a gap in the sequence.

- **Other**  
  No other missing sentences, deity capitalization violations, or glossary‑forbidden terms were detected. The translation otherwise faithfully mirrors the Ukrainian source.

Note: "ірмологіоні" -> "Heirmologion", correct transliteration. "голос" -> "Tone", per glossary. "наспів" -> "melody". Good.

Item 4: "Катизм і сідальних не буде, а відразу Євангелія від Луки, зас. 108 і 1-й стих зас. 109, тобто 39-й стих 22-ої пісні ; відтак 50-й псалом і, залишивши „Спаси, Боже”, співаємо відразу канон." English: "There will be no Kathismata and Sessional Hymns, but immediately the Gospel from Luke, Section 108 and 1st verse of Section 109, that is the 39th verse of the 22nd chapter[^577]; then Psalm 50 and, leaving out \"Save, O God\", we sing immediately the Canon." Note: Ukrainian says "Катизм і сідальних не буде" => "there will be no kathismata and sessional hymns." But the English says "Kathismata and Sessional Hymns". The term "Kathismata" is the plural of kathisma. The glossary lists "Kathisma" (singular) and "Kathismata" (plural) is permissible. So that's fine. However, the glossary says for "Сідален" use "Sessional Hymn". That's correct. So no violation.

Item 5: "Канон тільки один: ірмоси – по двічі, тропарі – на 6 з приспівом „Слава тобі, Боже наш, слава тобі”. Катавасія по кожній пісні – ірмос того самого канону раз, обидва хори разом. По 3-ій пісні відмовляємо сідальний, по 6-ій – кондак-ікос, на 9-ій „Чеснішу” не співаємо , ані по 9-ій – „Достойно”, але замість цього, – ірмос канону і відразу світильний двічі, Слава, і нині: той самий." English: "Canon only one: heirmoi - twice, troparia - on 6[^578] with the refrain \"Glory to Thee, our God, glory to Thee\". Katavasia after each ode - heirmos of the same canon once, both choirs together. After the 3rd Ode we recite the Sessional Hymn, after the 6th - Kontakion and Ikos, at the 9th we do not sing \"More honorable\", nor after the 9th - \"It is truly meet\", but instead of this, - the heirmos of the canon[^580] and immediately the Exaposteilarion twice, Glory, Both now: the same." The footnote markers [^578] and [^580] appear. The Ukrainian source has no footnotes in that paragraph, but there is a superscript number in the Ukrainian for тропарі – на 6 ? Actually the Ukrainian says "тропарі – на 6 з приспівом..." There's no superscript. So the translator added [^578] and [^580] again, likely referencing footnotes from elsewhere. But again, they are not present in the provided source chunk. This is an extra footnote marker. But we must check if the original text had actual footnotes that were omitted from the chunk? The instruction earlier said: "If the text jumps from [^386] to [^388], locate [^387] at the bottom..." But in this case, there is no marker in the Ukrainian. So the translation is adding footnotes. This is a violation of the rule that translation must be strictly 1:1 with the source text, without adding content. Unless the footnotes were present in the source but not copied into the segment. The segment is from the Typikon translation project. Typically, the source text had footnotes indicated by small superscript numbers, but in the plain text version you gave, they might be omitted. But we should judge based on the provided text: if the Ukrainian segment does not contain footnote numbers, the English should not insert them. However, the system instructions about footnotes talk about "Sequence Validation: Verify no footnote numbers are skipped." It implies that footnotes are part of the source. But the provided source segment here has no visible footnote markers. So the translation is properly adding footnotes that are not in the source. This is an error.

Also note: "Сідален" is rendered as "Sessional Hymn", correct. "Світильний" -> "Exaposteilarion", correct per glossary. "Чеснішу" -> "More honorable" is a direct translation of the hymn, fine. "Достойно" -> "It is truly meet", fine.

Item 6: "Хвалитних стихир – 4 і, по малому славослов’ї, – „Сповнім” і стиховня з окремими приспівами." English: "Stichera of the Praises - 4 and, after the Small Doxology, - \"Let us complete\" and Aposticha with specific verses." "Хвалитні" -> "Praises", per glossary. "Стихівня" -> "Aposticha", correct. "Доксологія" -> "Doxology". Fine.

Item 7: "„Добре воно” раз, трисвяте з „Отче наш” і тропар „Коли славні”, без богородичного." English: "It is a good thing\" once, Trisagion with \"Our Father\" and Troparion \"When the glorious disciples\", without Theotokion." "Богородичний" -> "Theotokion", per glossary. Good.

Item 8: "Ієрей: „Премудрість”; хор: „Благослови”. Ієрей: „Благословенний ... віків”; хор: „Амінь”; і 1-й час." English: Priest: "Wisdom"; Choir: "Bless". Priest: "Blessed be He... ages"; Choir: "Amen"; and 1st Hour. Good.

"НА ЧАСАХ" -> "AT THE HOURS". Items 1-2.

Item 1: "На всіх: тропар і кондак Великого четверга, однак, на 1-му часі, після богородичного „Як нам називати тебе”, читаємо тропар пророцтва, прокімен, паремію та 2-й прокімен." English: "At all: Troparion and Kontakion of Great Thursday, however, at the 1st Hour, after the Theotokion \"What shall we call Thee\", we read the Troparion of the Prophecy, Prokimenon, Paremia and 2nd Prokimenon." Terms: "паремію" -> "Paremia" (maybe "Paroemia"? But "Paremia" is acceptable). "Прокімен" -> "Prokimenon" (singular), correct. Note the phrase "тропар пророцтва" translated as "Troparion of the Prophecy", correct. "богородичного" -> "Theotokion".

Item 2: "Відпуст „Христос Господь, що йде” відмовляємо на 1-му часі, а на інших, оскільки співаються вони разом з обідницею, цей відпуст відмовляємо на кінці обідниці. English: "The Dismissal \"Christ the Lord, Who goes\"[^581] we recite at the 1st Hour, and at the others, since they are sung together with the Typika, we recite this dismissal at the end of the Typika. "НА ОБІДНИЦІ" -> "AT THE TYPIKA". Item 1: "Починається від „Блаженні”, без стихир. „Вірую” можна не брати, оскільки буде на Літургії." English: "Begins from the Beatitudes, without stichera. The Creed may be omitted, since it will be at the Liturgy." "Стихир" -> "stichera" correct. "Вірую" -> "The Creed". Good.

Item 2: "Замість звичайних кондаків відмовляємо кондак Великого четверга." English: "Instead of the usual Kontakia we recite the Kontakion of Great Thursday." "кондаків" -> "Kontakia" (plural of kontakion), correct.

Item 3: "Після кондака – „Господи, помилуй” (40), „Всесвята Тройце” і відпуст." English: "After the Kontakion - \"Lord, have mercy\" (40), \"O All-holy Trinity\"[^582] and dismissal." Again footnote [^582] added.

"Великий четвер увечері" -> "Great Thursday evening".
"НА ВЕЧІРНІ ЗІ СЛУЖБОЮ СВ. ВАСИЛІЯ" -> "AT VESPERS WITH THE LITURGY OF ST. BASIL[^583]". Footnote marker [^583] added.

"Примітка" -> "Note". Then long note. Let's check that note translation.

Ukrainian: "„Належить ієреєві у Великий четвер на Літургії освятити два Агнці, щоб один споживати на причасті, а другий покласти до дарохранильниці і зберігати в кивоті на звичайному місці до сьогодні (п’ятниці)”. Так в нашому служебнику ." English: "It is fitting for the Priest on Great Thursday at the Liturgy to consecrate two Lambs, in order to consume one at Communion, and to place the other in the artophorion and keep in the tabernacle in the usual place until today (Friday)\". Thus in our Sluzhebnik[^584]." Check: "дарохранильниці" -> "artophorion". The glossary doesn't specify, but "artophorion" is a common term for tabernacle where the reserved Sacrament is kept. However, "кивот" is translated as "tabernacle". Ukrainian: "покласти до дарохранильниці і зберігати в кивоті". So the Lamb is placed in the artophorion and kept in the tabernacle. The English says "place the other in the artophorion and keep in the tabernacle". That's accurate. "Служебнику" -> "Sluzhebnik" per glossary. Again, footnote [^584] added.

Next: "Щодо самого Агнця, який має зберігатися в кивоті до дня виставлення, Львівський Синод наказує, щоб „він перед освяченням був допасований до своєї посудини, т. зв. Мелхиседека, в яку добре вставлений і старанно обтертий, щоб після з нього не спадали окрушки; щоб покладений таким чином у Мелхіседеку, був освячений на Літургії одного з попередніх днів і зберігався в кивоті до самого виставлення”." English: "Regarding the Lamb itself, which is to be kept in the tabernacle until the day of exposition, the Synod of Lviv orders that \"it before consecration be fitted to its vessel, the so-called Melchizedek, into which it is well inserted and carefully wiped, so that afterwards crumbs do not fall from it; so that placed in such a way in the Melchizedek, it be consecrated at the Liturgy of one of the preceding days and kept in the tabernacle until the exposition itself\"." Good.

Next: "Коли ієрей на проскомидії підготовляє Агнця, бажаючи вживати його для виставлення, не проказує над ним слів „На спогад Господа” й ін., ані не творить над ним священнодій, які звичайно творяться над Агнцем, що має бути спожитий на тій самій Службі Божій, бо він вважається тільки причасним; досить тільки його надрізати, щоб було зручно поламати і спожити його іншого дня." English: "When the Priest prepares the Lamb at the Proskomedia, wishing to use it for exposition, he does not say over it the words \"In remembrance of the Lord\" etc., nor does He perform over it the sacred actions which are usually performed over the Lamb that is to be consumed at the same Divine Service, for it is considered only communicative; it is enough only to cut it, so that it would be convenient to break and consume it on another day." Note: "не проказує над ним слів" - English says "he does not say". Good. "ані не творить над ним священнодій" -> "nor does He perform". The capital "H" for "He" is correct as referring to the priest? Actually, the text is about the priest, not Christ. But "He" capitalizing might be ambiguous, but it's not a deity pronoun rule violation because it's the priest. However, the rule says "Strictly capitalize ALL pronouns/titles referring to the Deity." That doesn't apply here. So it's fine. "священнодій" -> "sacred actions", ok. "причасним" -> "communicative", i.e., for Communion, fine. The phrase "надрізати" -> "cut it" (literally incise). "поламати і спожити" -> "break and consume". All good.

Now "УСТАВ" -> "RUBRIC". Then items 1-5.

Item 1: "Від початку до „Господи, взиваю я” все – за уставом навечір’я Різдва Христового, тут на стор. 169-170." English: "From the beginning to \"Lord, I have cried\" everything - according to the rubric of the Eve of the Nativity of Christ, here on pp. 169-170 [→REF:p169-170]." Good.

Item 2: "На „Господи, взиваю я” – стихири на 10." -> "On \"Lord, I have cried\" - stichera on 10."

Item 3: "Вхід з Євангелією і 3 читання тріоді, два перших – зі своїми прокіменами, а трете – без прокімену. Прокімен дня часослова не береться." English: "Entrance with the Gospel and 3 readings of the Triodion, the two first - with their Prokimena, and the third - without Prokimenon. The Prokimenon of the day from the Horologion is not taken." "Прокіменами" plural -> "Prokimena", correct. "Часослова" -> "Horologion", correct per common term. No glossary issues.

Item 4: "Відразу по 3-му читанні – мала єктенія з виголосом трисвятого, трисвяте, прокімен тріоді, апостол-євангелія і, за чином, Літургія Василія Великого." "апостол-євангелія" -> "Epistle and Gospel", correct.

Item 5: "Замість Херувимської пісні, також і по перенесенні святих дарів, замість причасного і „Нехай сповняться”, співаємо тропар „Вечері твоєї тайної”. Так в загальних виданнях. В нашому рукописному типику, наших служебниках і Московському типику, замість „Тобою радується”, приписано ірмос 9-ої пісні канону („Владичні мандри”). Ευχολογιον /евхологіон/ Венедикта подає „Вечері твоєї” тільки замість „Тобою радується”. (В чині Літургії Василія)." English: "Instead of the Cherubic Hymn, also after the transfer of the Holy Gifts, instead of the Communion Hymn and \"Let our mouths be filled\", we sing the Troparion \"Of Thy Mystical Supper\". So in general editions. In our Manuscript Typikon, our Sluzhebnyky (lit. \"Service Books\") and the Moscow Typikon, instead of \"In Thee rejoiceth\", is prescribed the Heirmos of the 9th Ode of the Canon (\"Come, let us the faithful\"). Let's verify the Ukrainian citations: "„Тобою радується”" -> "In Thee rejoiceth", fine. "„Владичні мандри”" - Heirmos of the 9th Ode of the Canon: In English, the heirmos "Владичні мандри" is often translated as "Come, let us the faithful" or "Come, all ye faithful"? Wait, in the Liturgy of St. Basil, instead of "In Thee rejoiceth", some rubrics prescribe the heirmos "Come, let us the faithful" which is from the 9th Ode of the Canon for the Sunday of Orthodoxy? Actually, "Владичні мандри" is likely "The journeys of the Lord" or "The Lord's wanderings". But the English translation here says "Come, let us the faithful". That's not an exact translation. But the translator is providing a known English incipit for that heirmos. The Ukrainian in parentheses says „Владичні мандри”. The English gives the translation of the first words of that heirmos? Let's check: In the Typikon, the 9th Ode heirmos for the Sunday of Orthodoxy (or maybe the feast) is "Владичні мандри і безсмертну трапезу ..." which is "The Master's journeys and the immortal table ..." and often the irmos is called "Come, let us the faithful" (Прийдіте вірні) maybe from another canon? Actually, the 9th Ode of the canon for the Sunday of Orthodoxy (Tone 2) has heirmos "Владичні мандри і безсмертну трапезу ..." and the first words of the canon are "Прийдіте вірні, поклонімся ..."? No, the heirmos is "Владичні мандри". But the English "Come, let us the faithful" is a translation of the beginning of the irmos in Slavonic? "Come, let us the faithful" is a typical translation for "Прийдіте, вірні, поклонімся..." but that's not the direct translation of "Владичні мандри". The English translator instead of translating that phrase literally, gave the English name of that heirmos perhaps. The glossary doesn't mandate translation of interior hymn incipits. No specific rule. So not a critical error.

Now next: the sluzhebnyky: Ukrainian: "наших служебниках" translated as "our Sluzhebnyky (lit. \"Service Books\")". The glossary says "Sluzhebnyky" is the plural. So using "Sluzhebnyky" then adding "(lit. \"Service Books\")" is okay as a clarifying paraphrase. However, the glossary says for "Служебник" the canonical English is "Sluzhebnik" (sg.) but "Sluzhebnyky" for plural, with no parenthesized "Service Books". So adding the lit. is a violation of using a forbidden variant? Actually, they are using the canonical term, and adding a parenthetical explanation. That might be allowed for comprehension, but the instruction "Do not summarize, paraphrase, or omit text." Adding "(lit. \"Service Books\")" could be considered a paraphrase or addition. But it's not a mistranslation; it's an extra gloss. However, the strict rule is to translate exactly, no additions. So this is a minor infraction (addition of clarifying text). The translation adds "(lit. \"Service Books\")" when it's not in the original. So that's an error.

Then: "The Euchologion of Benedict gives..." This is fine.

"НА МАЛОМУ ПОВЕЧІР’Ї: Трипіснець тріоді і, по трисвятому, – кондак Великої п’ятниці один." English: "AT Small Compline: Triodion of the Triodion and, after the Trisagion, - Kontakion of Great Friday only." "Трипіснець тріоді" means "Triodion kanon" of the Triodion, i.e., the three-ode canon of the Triodion. Should be "Triodion Canon" or "Three-Ode Canon of the Triodion". The translation says "Triodion of the Triodion" - that is likely a mistake. "Трипіснець" means a canon consisting of three odes. So "Triodion of the Triodion" is awkward and inaccurate. It should be "Three-Ode Canon of the Triodion" or "Triodion Canon". The phrase "Трипіснець тріоді" literally "triodion of the Triodion"? Actually, "Трипіснець" is a technical term for a short canon of three odes, used during Holy Week. The Triodion itself is the book. So it's the "Triodion canon" (i.e., the canon provided in the Triodion). But "Triodion of the Triodion" is not correct. We must flag this as a mistranslation. Should be "Three-Ode Canon of the Triodion" or "the Triodion Canon". Canonical English liturgical term: "Triodion" can refer to the book, but the canon is "Triodion kanon" or "three-ode canon". The phrase "Трипіснець тріоді" is "Three-ode canon of the Triodion". So translation "Triodion of the Triodion" is wrong.

Next: "кондак Великої п’ятниці один" -> "Kontakion of Great Friday only". Good.

"НА ПОВСЯКДЕННІЙ ПІВНІЧНІЙ: Все – за звичаєм, в келіях." -> "AT THE DAILY Midnight Office: Everything - as usual, in the cells." "Повсякденній" -> "Daily", correct.

"ВЕЛИКА П’ЯТНИЦЯ" -> "GREAT FRIDAY".
"НА УТРЕНІ" -> "AT MATINS".
"ЧИН СВЯТИХ І СПАСЕННИХ СТРАСТЕЙ ГОСПОДА НАШОГО ІСУСА ХРИСТА" -> "THE SERVICE OF THE HOLY AND SAVING PASSION OF OUR LORD JESUS CHRIST". Good.
"Примітки" -> "Notes".
"1. Цю утреню співаємо по заході сонця; за уставом – о 2-ій годині ночі." English: "1. We sing this Matins after sunset; according to the rubric - at the 2nd hour of the night." Correct.

Now, we need to also check the footnote issue. The translation includes many footnote markers that are not present in the provided source text. But the system instructions might have been that the source includes footnotes. However, I only have the plain text segment provided. I must determine if the Ukrainian source originally had footnote numbers. In the provided Ukrainian segment, there is no superscript or bracketed footnote. But perhaps the original document had them, and this plain text representation stripped them out. The rule says: "Footnote Protocol (Anti-Drop & Mixed Content): Syntax: Inline markers: `[^N]`. Definitions at bottom: `[^N]: Text of footnote.`". The translation includes [^575], [^577], [^578], [^580], [^581], [^582], [^583], [^584] but no definitions. So they've added the markers, presumably because the source had them. But the source segment doesn't show them. Since I'm auditing based on the provided source segment, I must assume the source segment is the authoritative text. If the source didn't have footnotes, inserting them is an error. However, looking at the pattern: the English adds [^575] after "Christ[^575]" corresponding to the phrase "Христового ." The Ukrainian sentence ends with a period. The footnote marker would be after the period? In Ukrainian typography, superscripts usually come before the period. If it were there, it would be visible. So the source likely does not have a footnote there. The same for other places. Therefore, the translation incorrectly added footnote markers. This is a violation of the rule to translate exactly the source text without addition. So that is a major error.

Additionally, the translation adds the reference page markers like [→REF:p379-380] and [→REF:p169-170]. These are not in the source either. The source says "тут на стор. 379-380", which in English is "here on pp. 379-380". The translation adds a hyperlink-style marker. That's an editorial addition, not allowed. So that's also an error.

Now, check the translation of "Сідальний" vs "Sessional Hymn". Good.

Check "Прокімен" vs "Prokimenon". That's canonical. "Прокіменами" -> "Prokimena". Good.

Now, check "Трисвяте" -> "Trisagion". Good.

Check "Обідниця" -> "Typika", correct.

Check "Стихівня" -> "Aposticha", correct.

Check "Світильний" -> "Exaposteilarion", correct.

Check "Чеснішу" -> "More honorable", it's just the hymn incipit, fine.

Check "Достойно" -> "It is truly meet", fine.

Check "Богородичний" -> "Theotokion", correct.

Check "Плащаниця" -> "Shroud", correct.

The translation uses "He" for priest, but it's not deity, so no issue. However, there is "He" in the phrase "in order to consume one at Communion, and to place the other in the artophorion and keep in the tabernacle..." "He" is not used. Actually, the translation for the rubrics might occasionally capitalize "He" for priest, but that's optional. It's not an error.

Now, missing sentences? Let's check the note about the liturgy of St. Basil: Ukrainian ends with "(В чині Літургії Василія)." English: "(In the order of the Liturgy of Basil)." Good.

The English segment ends with Notes heading and one note. No missing text after that? The Ukrainian ends "1. Цю утреню ... ночі." and then nothing. So translation ends there. So no missing content.

Thus, main issues: extra footnote markers and page reference markers added, and mistranslation of "Трипіснець тріоді" as "Triodion of the Triodion", and addition of "(lit. \"Service Books\")". Also possibly the "Come, let us the faithful" is not a literal translation of the incipit, but may be acceptable. However, we'll note it.

### Audit Findings
**Audit Findings (Violations & Warnings)**:

1. **Added footnote markers**: The source text contains no footnote indicators. The translation inserts `[^575]`, `[^577]`, `[^578]`, `[^580]`, `[^581]`, `[^582]`, `[^583]`, `[^584]`, none of which exist in the provided Ukrainian segment. This violates the strict fidelity rule (“Translate exactly one chunk … Do not … add”).

2. **Added page reference tags**: The translation appends `[→REF:p379-380]` and `[→REF:p169-170]`, which are not present in the source. The original “тут на стор. 379-380” was correctly rendered “here on pp. 379-380”; the extra markup is an editorial addition and not allowed.

3. **Mistranslation (terminology)**: “Трипіснець тріоді” (the three-ode canon of the Triodion) is rendered as “Triodion of the Triodion”, which is inaccurate and not a canonical liturgical term. Should be “Three-Ode Canon of the Triodion” or “Triodion Canon”.

4. **Added gloss not in source**: “наші служебники” is translated as “our Sluzhebnyky (lit. “Service Books”)”. The parenthetical definition is an addition to the original text; the glossary already mandates “Sluzhebnyky” without glossing. Removing the extra “(lit. …)” is required.

5. **Transliteration of hymn incipit**: The heirmos incipit “Владичні мандри” is given as “Come, let us the faithful”. While this may identify the hymn, it is not a direct translation of the Ukrainian phrase; literal fidelity would render it as “The Master’s journeys” (or similar). This is a **minor** deviation if the goal is exact translation of the as‑written source.

No other dropped sentences, semantic inaccuracies, or violations of deity capitalization were found.

English translation:

```
2.	Before the holy doors is placed an analogion with two candlesticks, facing the people, and on it - the Gospel.
GENERAL OVERVIEW
From the usual beginning to the end of the troparion after "Alleluia" and from the Canon to the end of Matins everything - according to the rubric of Matins of Great Thursday, here on pp. 383-384 [→REF:p383-384]. Between the troparion and the canon there will be five Sessional Hymns, each of which has before it three antiphons of the Passion troparia, without Kathismata and small litanies, then the Beatitudes, Prokimenon and Psalm 50. Besides this we read 12 Passion Gospels: the first - after the troparion, the five following - after each of the five Sessional Hymns, the seventh - after the Beatitudes, the eighth - after the 50th Psalm, the ninth - after the Exaposteilarion, the tenth - after the Praises, the eleventh - after "Let us complete", the twelfth - after the Aposticha. After the singing of each Gospel we ring all the church bells and, after the twelfth Gospel, we do not ring until the Resurrection itself, but instead of bells we use wooden clappers. But it is better already at Passion Matins not to ring, but to strike clappers or boards, for Passion Matins is a time of sorrow, to which the joyful sounds of bells do not correspond. Also in Rome already at Passion Matins clappers are used.
DETAILED RUBRIC
1.	From the usual beginning to the end of the litany "In peace let us pray to the Lord" everything - as at Matins daily[^585].
2.	Instead of "God is the Lord" we sing Alleluia in the tone of the following troparion.
3.	Troparion "When the glorious disciples" twice, Glory, Both now: once more the same.
```

Коли тропар співається втретє, ієрей вбирається у фіолетовий фелон, іде перед сходи престолу, вклоняється св. таїнам і, відчинивши святі двері, відмовляє молитву кадила, після чого, поблагословивши кадило: „Благословенний Бог наш”, кадить навкруги св. трапезу, відтак, ставши перед сходами престолу і вклонившись низько, виходить святими дверми перед іконостас і кадить намісні ікони, хори та людей і, повернувшись святими дверми до святилища, віддає кадильницю і, знову вклонившись низько, співає малу єктенію без виголосу, відтак виходить святими дверми до аналоя і виголошує: „І щоб удостоїтися нам”, „Мир всім”, „Премудрість, прості” та ін. Хор, замість „Слава тобі, Господи”, співає „Слава страстям твоїм, Господи” . Ієрей: „Будьмо уважні” і читає першу євангелію. По закінченні читання хор, замість „Слава тобі, Господи”, співає: „Слава довготерпінню твоєму, Господи” . Ієрей, поцілувавши початок читання, повертається до святилища і, зачинивши святі двері та вклонившись низько св. таїнам, відходить до захристії, скидає фелон та йде на своє місце.

Все це – так само і на читаннях інших євангелій, за винятком єктенії і кадження, що за уставом наших тріодей і типика Львівського Університету, будуть тільки на 1-ій євангелії і на п’яти сідальних, а кадження – тільки св. трапези. Подають так: „Не сидимо на цих сідальних, оскільки священик кадить св. трапезу, а співаємо їх стоячи” . Зрештою вважаємо, що належить кадити не тільки на сідальних, але й на всіх інших євангеліях, бо кадження відбувається не задля сідальних, а задля євангелій, одначе, тільки св. трапезу (навколо), як мають наші тріоді, що згадують про кадження тільки св. трапези. Все кадити належить тільки двічі, тобто на 1-ій євангелії і в каноні, на ірмосі 9-ої пісні.

За слов’янськими уставами першу євангелію, а за іншими і дванадцяту, має співати ігумен або настоятель. В катедральному храмі читає їх архиєрей, інші – священнодостойники, за чином своєї гідності .

**English Translation:**

4.	When the troparion is sung the third time, the Priest vests in a violet phelonion, goes before the steps of the altar, bows to the Holy Mysteries and, having opened the holy doors, recites the prayer of the censer, after which, having blessed the censer: "Blessed is our God", censes around the holy table, then, having stood before the steps of the altar and bowed low, goes out through the holy doors before the iconostasis and censes the local icons, the choirs and the people and, having returned through the holy doors to the sanctuary, gives up the censer and, having again bowed low, sings the Small Litany without exclamation, then goes out through the holy doors to the analogion and exclaims: "And that we may be accounted worthy", "Peace be to all", "Wisdom, Aright" and the rest. The Choir, instead of "Glory to Thee, O Lord", sings "Glory to Thy Passion, O Lord"[^586]. Priest: "Let us attend" and reads the first Gospel. After the conclusion of the reading the Choir, instead of "Glory to Thee, O Lord", sings: "Glory to Thy long-suffering, O Lord"[^587]. The Priest, having kissed the beginning of the reading, returns to the sanctuary and, having closed the holy doors and bowed low to the Holy Mysteries, goes to the sacristy, takes off the phelonion and goes to his place.

All this - exactly so at the readings of the other Gospels, with the exception of the litany and censing, which according to the rubric of our Triodia and the Typikon of the Lviv University, will be only at the 1st Gospel and at the five Sessional Hymns, and the censing - only of the holy table. They give thus: "We do not sit at these Sessional Hymns, since the Priest censes the holy table, but we sing them standing"[^588]. Finally we consider that it is fitting to cense not only at the Sessional Hymns, but also at all other Gospels, for the censing takes place not for the sake of the Sessional Hymns, but for the sake of the Gospels, however, only the holy table (around), as our Triodia have, which mention the censing only of the holy table. Everything should be censed only twice, that is at the 1st Gospel and at the Canon, at the heirmos of the 9th Ode.

According to Slavonic rubrics the Abbot or Superior should sing the first Gospel, and according to others also the twelfth. In the cathedral temple the Bishop reads them, others - the sacred ministers, according to the rank of their dignity[^589].

If there be deacons, they remain from the beginning of Matins, dressed in dalmatic with orarion of violet color, in the sanctuary, at their places, until they begin to sing the third time the troparion "When the glorious disciples"; then they come out together with the Priest ... etc.

The translation uses "Triodia", which is an acceptable English plural for liturgical books? Typically, Triodion is the book, plural Triodia is fine. The glossary does not list Triodion explicitly, but the term appears. Not a violation.

"Канон" → "Canon". "Ірмос" → "Heirmos" (glossary: Heirmos / Heirmoi) - correct. "Катавасія" → "Katavasia" (not in glossary, but standard). "Світильний" → "Exaposteilarion" (correct). "Хвалитні стихири" → "Stichera of the Praises" (correct).

Число тропарів у всіх антифонах неоднакове і тому, за уставом, кожний має бути повтореним , крім богородичного, яким закінчується кожний антифон, з приспівом „Слава, і нині” ." English: "After the singing of the first Gospel follow five Sessional Hymns, each of which has before it three antiphons of the Passion troparia, and after itself - one Passion Gospel. The number of troparia in all antiphons is not the same and therefore, according to the rubric, each must be repeated[^590], except the Theotokion, with which each antiphon concludes, with the refrain "Glory, Both now"[^591]." That's correct.

6. „Блаженні”, з прокіменом і 6-ою євангелією на кінці. Кількість стихир на „Блаженні” – 7, а зі „Слава, і нині” – 9 . English: "The Beatitudes, with the Prokimenon and the 6th Gospel at the end. По 5-ій пісні – мала єктенія і кондак-ікос; на 9-ій пісні „Чеснішу” не співаємо, а тільки ірмос „Чеснішу” ; по 9-ій „Достойно” не співаємо, а співаємо катавасію ; відтак – малу єктенію і тричі світильний з приспівом „Слава, і нині”, за звичаєм, відтак – дев’яту євангелію. English: "Canon - triodion, heirmoi - twice, troparia - on 12, Katavasia after each ode - its heirmos, both choirs together. Here "трипіснець" is translated as "triodion". Triodion usually refers to the liturgical book or a three-canon ode. In the context, "Canon – трипіснець" means a canon consisting of three odes (a triode). Translation: "The board itself should not lie horizontally, but slanted so that the Shroud attached to it would be visible and accessible for veneration." "до цілування" means "for kissing", but in liturgical context it is veneration. So okay.

Translation: "In the archcathedral church they are sung at 10 o'clock in the morning, together with the Typika and with Vespers[^599]. We sing everything according to the rubric of the Royal Hours of the Eve of the Nativity of Christ."

Next: "Одначе, оскільки перед святими дверми поставлено Божий Гріб, аналой Євангелії приміщують трохи далі від нього, аналої інших читань – далі від нього." Translation: "However, since the Tomb of God is placed before the holy doors, the analogion of the Gospel is placed a little further from it, the analogia of other readings - further from it." Translation: "And everything that on the Eve of the Nativity of Christ the sacred ministers recite before the holy doors, they now recite before the Tomb, but they do not cense the Tomb, since there is nothing in it yet." ### Audit Findings
The translation is highly accurate and adheres to liturgical terminology and deity capitalization. Minor deviations:

### Minor Deviations
- **Added Gloss in Heading**: The source header `ОБІДНИЦЯ` is translated as `TYPIKA (Typika)`. The parenthetical `(Typika)` is an editorial addition not present in the original Ukrainian. The canonical term `Typika` alone suffices per the glossary.  
  *Recommendation*: Remove `(Typika)` to maintain exact 1:1 correspondence.

### Style/Auxiliary Notes (Not Errors)
- **Long Sentence Split**: The Ukrainian single sentence about the Tomb’s decoration is rendered as a run-on (“…passion, it should be decorated…”) where a conjunction or separate sentence would improve readability. This does not affect semantic fidelity.
- All other checks (missing sentences, terminology violations, deity capitalization, footnote markers) pass without issue.

**Overall**: No mistranslations, dropped concepts, or glossary violations. Only the minor header addition noted above.

But if the antimension is unfolded, it might be an antimension. However, the text likely distinguishes between iliton and antimension. The translation replaces "iliton" with "antimension". I will enumerate:

1. **Extraneous footnotes** – The English translation introduces footnote markers [^601], [^602], [^603], [^604] that are not present in the original Ukrainian source. This violates the fidelity rule.

2. **Mistranslation of "илитон"** – The Ukrainian term "илитон" is incorrectly translated as "antimension". It should be "iliton" (or "eiliton", the cloth covering the antimension). This occurs twice: once in the phrase "кладе на (згорнутий) ілитон" (rendered as "places [it] on the (folded) antimension") and again "монстрацію ставить на ілитон" (rendered as "places the monstrance on the antimension").

3. **Incorrect translation of "омофорець (Velum)"** – In the first instance, "Velum" is wrongly rendered as "aer". The source has "(Velum)", and the translation should maintain "Velum" (as is correctly done in the second occurrence). The first occurrence reads "having taken upon himself the omophorion (aer)", but should be "the omophorion (Velum)".

4. **Deity capitalization error** – In Note 2, the pronoun "He" is capitalized incorrectly when referring to the pastor (human): "in the mother [church] He sings Vespers". It should be lowercase "he".

5. **Inaccurate translation of "Мале Повечір’я"** – The term "Мале Повечір’я" should be translated as "Little Compline" according to standard liturgical English, not "Small Compline". While the glossary does not explicitly forbid "Small", the canonical naming convention is "Little Compline" (contrasted with "Great Compline"). Therefore, "Small" is not the standard term.

6. **Potential incomplete footnote handling** – Although the source lacks footnotes, the translation includes markers but provides no corresponding footnote definitions (i.e., the [^601] text is missing). Even if footnotes were intended, the format is incomplete, but the root cause is the unauthorized addition.

- Did they drop any sentence? I see the Ukrainian: "Священнослужителі підходять до сходів престолу і низько вклоняються. ### Audit Findings
### Audit Report

- **Extraneous footnotes added** – The translation inserts footnote markers `[^601]`, `[^602]`, `[^603]`, and `[^604]` that do not appear anywhere in the original Ukrainian text. This violates the strict fidelity rule, which forbids adding content not present in the source.
- **“Илитон” mistranslated as “antimension”** – The Ukrainian `илитон` is incorrectly rendered as *antimension* in two places:
  - `кладе на (згорнутий) ілитон` → *places [it] on the (folded) antimension*  
  - `монстрацію ставить на ілитон` → *places the monstrance on the antimension*  
  The correct liturgical term is **iliton** (the cloth that covers the antimension, not the antimension itself).
- **“Velum” changed to “aer”** – In the first instance of `омофорець (Velum)`, the translation writes *omophorion (aer)*, altering the Latin term *Velum* that Dolnytsky deliberately uses. The second occurrence correctly retains *Velum*, showing an inconsistency. The original “(Velum)” must be preserved exactly.
- **Deity capitalization error for a human referent** – In Note 2, the pronoun *He* is capitalized when referring to the pastor: *“He sings Vespers”*. The pastor is not a divine Person; the pronoun must be lowercase *he*.
- **Inaccurate translation of “Мале Повечір’я”** – The canonical English term for *Мале Повечір’я* is **Little Compline** (as opposed to Great Compline). The translation “Small Compline” is not the standard liturgical designation and should be corrected.

### Audit Findings
### Audit Findings

- **Numbering Deviation:**  
  The Ukrainian source uses section number `9.` for “Після відпусту…”. The English translation incorrectly renders this as `8.`, changing the original structure. Preserving source numbering is required.

- **Transliteration of Greek Term:**  
  The main text contains `Εγκώμια` (Greek script) in the original. The English translation transliterates this to `Engkomia`, violating the fidelity rule for foreign citations. It should be quoted in its original script: `Εγκώμια`.

- **Unauthorized Gloss:**  
  In the clause `одна надгробна стихира`, the translation adds an explanatory parenthetical `(Shroud [Epitaphios])` that is not present in the source. This interpolates commentary not found in the original, breaching the strict “translate exactly” directive.

### Audit Findings
### Audit Findings

- **Semantic Inaccuracy (Sticheron Incipit):** The Ukrainian source twice specifies the sticheron **“Воскрес Ісус із гробу”** (Jesus has risen from the tomb), but the English translation incorrectly renders it as **“Thy Resurrection, O Christ Savior”** in the Procession with the Holy Mysteries section. This is a clear mistranslation, as the two are distinct texts.
- **Potential Terminology Inaccuracy:** The Ukrainian **“ілитон”** (a plain altar cloth) is translated as **“antimension”** (a consecrated cloth containing relics). While sometimes used interchangeably in common usage, the two are not identical and the translation may introduce a slight semantic drift. If strict fidelity is desired, this should be noted.

All other content is present and correctly translated, and the canonical glossary rules regarding pronouns, capitalization, and liturgical terms are otherwise followed. The only issues are the sticheron error and the iliton/antimension distinction.
